"""Per-head CUDA paged attention decode kernel.

Architecture: one thread block per (batch, query_head), 128 threads.
Each thread handles one element of D, reduces qk across threads.
"""
import math
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

def _make_scale(head_dim: int) -> float:
    return 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)

_module = None

def _compile():
    # Put ALL the code in the CUDA source. No C++ wrapper needed.
    # We define the kernel AND the C++ interface function in the .cu file.
    CUDA_SRC = r"""
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <cuda_bf16.h>
#include <math.h>
#include <torch/extension.h>

using bfloat = __nv_bfloat16;

__global__ void __launch_bounds__(128) paged_decode_kernel(
    bfloat* __restrict__ Out,
    const bfloat* __restrict__ Q,
    const bfloat* __restrict__ KV,
    const int* __restrict__ BlockTable,
    const int* __restrict__ SeqLens,
    int B, int H, int Hkv, int D, int P, float scale,
    int stride_qb, int stride_qo,
    int stride_kvb, int stride_kvs, int stride_kvh, int stride_kvo,
    int stride_ob, int stride_oo,
    int stride_bt_row
) {
    int pid_b = blockIdx.x;
    int pid_h = blockIdx.y;
    int tid = threadIdx.x;

    int pid_hkv = pid_h / (H / Hkv);
    int seq_len = SeqLens[pid_b];
    int num_pages = (seq_len + P - 1) / P;

    // Early exit
    if (tid >= D) return;

    // Load Q element
    float q_val = __bfloat162float(Q[pid_b * stride_qb + pid_h * stride_qo + tid]);

    // Accumulators
    float acc_num_val = 0.0f;
    float acc_denom = 1e-30f;
    float acc_max = -1e30f;

    // Warp count
    int num_warps = (D + 31) / 32;
    int my_warp = tid / 32;

    for (int pg = 0; pg < num_pages; pg++) {
        int page_id = BlockTable[pid_b * stride_bt_row + pg];

        int tok_end = min((pg + 1) * P, seq_len);
        int tok_start = pg * P;

        for (int t = tok_start; t < tok_end; t++) {
            int local_t = t - tok_start;

            // Load K[tid]
            int k_base = page_id * stride_kvb + local_t * stride_kvs + pid_hkv * stride_kvh;
            float k_val = __bfloat162float(KV[k_base + tid * stride_kvo]);

            // Partial dot product
            float partial = q_val * k_val;

            // Intra-warp reduction
            #pragma unroll
            for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1)
                partial += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, partial, offset);

            // Each warp leader writes its sum to shared memory
            __shared__ float warp_sum[4];
            if (tid % 32 == 0)
                warp_sum[tid / 32] = partial;
            __syncthreads();

            // Compute full qk reduction
            float qk = 0.0f;
            for (int w = 0; w < num_warps; w++)
                qk += warp_sum[w];
            qk *= scale;

            // Load V[tid]
            float v_val = __bfloat162float(KV[k_base + D + tid * stride_kvo]);

            // Online softmax (consistent across all threads)
            float old_max = acc_max;
            float new_max = fmaxf(old_max, qk);
            float exp_v = __expf(qk - new_max);
            float rescale = __expf(old_max - new_max);

            acc_num_val = acc_num_val * rescale + exp_v * v_val;
            acc_denom = acc_denom * rescale + exp_v;
            acc_max = new_max;
        }
    }

    // Write output
    Out[pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oo + tid] = __float2bfloat16(acc_num_val / acc_denom);
}

// PyTorch binding
void paged_attention_forward(
    torch::Tensor out,
    torch::Tensor query,
    torch::Tensor kv_cache,
    torch::Tensor block_table,
    torch::Tensor seq_lens,
    float scale)
{
    int B = query.size(0);
    int H = query.size(1);
    int D = query.size(2);
    int Hkv = kv_cache.size(2);
    int P = kv_cache.size(1);
    int stride_bt_row = block_table.stride(0);

    dim3 grid(B, H);
    dim3 block(128, 1, 1);
    paged_decode_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(
        (bfloat*)out.data_ptr(),
        (const bfloat*)query.data_ptr(),
        (const bfloat*)kv_cache.data_ptr(),
        block_table.data_ptr<int>(),
        seq_lens.data_ptr<int>(),
        B, H, Hkv, D, P, scale,
        query.stride(0), query.stride(1),
        kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2), kv_cache.stride(3),
        out.stride(0), out.stride(1),
        stride_bt_row);
}

PYBIND11_MODULE(TORCH_EXTENSION_NAME, m) {
    m.def("paged_attention_forward", &paged_attention_forward, "paged_attention_forward");
}
"""

    return load_inline(
        name="paged_attn_cuda_v5",
        cpp_sources='',
        cuda_sources=CUDA_SRC,
        extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"],
        verbose=False,
    )

def _get_module():
    global _module
    if _module is None:
        _module = _compile()
    return _module

class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, batch, num_heads, num_kv_heads, head_dim, seq_len, page_size):
        super().__init__()
        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0
        self.batch = batch
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
        self.head_dim = head_dim
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.page_size = page_size
        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)

    def forward(self, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens):
        B, H, D = self.batch, self.num_heads, self.head_dim
        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads

        out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=query.device)
        _get_module().paged_attention_forward(out, query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens, self.scale)
        return out


def get_inputs():
    import reference
    return reference.get_inputs()


def get_init_inputs():
    import reference
    return reference.get_init_inputs()
The problem: `torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline` compiles the .cpp file as C++ (not CUDA C++), so `<<<` kernel launch syntax is invalid. I need to put **everything** in the .cuda file or use the kernel launch wrapper defined in CUDA code only:

1: """Naive PyTorch paged-attention decode reference (correctness oracle, not SOTA).
2: 
3: Single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim)
4: and attends over a KV cache of `seq_len[b]` tokens stored as fixed-size pages in
5: a global pool. Pages for batch element b are listed in `block_table[b]`.
6: 
7: The reference performs the slow path:
8:   1. Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element.
9:   2. Repeat KV heads for grouped-query (broadcast num_kv_heads -> num_heads).

11:

2: display_name: "Paged Attention Decode"
3: precision: bf16
4: regime: memory  # decode is bandwidth-bound (KV cache streamed once per token)
5: 
6: # Effective FLOPs per call: QK^T + softmax*V across all batches/heads/seq.
7: # Sum-formula evaluated per-shape; the benchmark substitutes batch/num_heads/etc.
8: # 2 * B * H * L * D for QK^T plus 2 * B * H * L * D for AV  =>  4 * B * H * L * D

<content>
1: I need you to write a paged attention decode kernel for the RTX PRO 6000 (SM120 Blackwell, GDDR7, 1.8 TB/s). The reference implementation is in reference.py and your kernel goes in solution.py. You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.
2: 
3: This is single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim) and attends over a KV cache of seq_len[b] tokens stored as fixed-size pages in a global pool, with block_table[b] listing which pages belong to batch element b. The KV cache is laid out as (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2) where the last dim packs [K | V] so a single gather pulls both. You return the bf16 output of shape (batch, num_heads, head_dim). Correctness tolerance is 0.02 abs/rel on bf16/fp16. The shapes you have to handle are batch=8 num_heads=32 num_kv_heads=8 head_dim=128 seq_len=1024 page_size=16 (Llama-3 8B-style decode), batch=32 num_heads=32 num_kv_heads=8 head_dim=128 seq_len=2048 page_size=16 (server-batched decode), batch=4 num_heads=64 num_kv_heads=8 head_dim=128 seq_len=4096 page_size=16 (Llama-3 70B GQA wide ratio with long context), batch=16 num_heads=32 num_kv_heads=8 head_dim=128

30:             return x

+"""Custom Triton paged attention decode kernel.
+
+Layout:
+  query:      (batch, num_heads, head_dim)             bf16
+  kv_cache:   (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)  bf16
+              last dim packs [K | V] so a single gather pulls both
+  block_table: (batch, max_blocks)                     int32
+  seq_lens:   (batch,)                                 int32
+
+Output: bf16 (batch, num_heads, head_dim)
+
+Strategy:
+  One program per (batch, kv_head). Each program:
+    1. Loads block_table[b] pointers for this batch.
+    2. Iterates over pages, loading K and V blocks from the page cache.
+    3. For each head in the GQA group, computes QK^T dot product.
+    4. Accumulates online softmax numerator and denominator.
+  We vectorize the head_dim dimension.
+"""
+import math
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _paged_decode_kernel(
+    # Output: (batch, num_heads, head_dim)
+    Out,
+    # Inputs
+    Q,
+    KVC,
+    BlockTable,
+    SeqLens,
+    # Strides
+    stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_qd,
+    stride_kc_b, stride_kc_s, stride_kc_h, stride_kc_d,
+    stride_bt_b, stride_bt_s,
+    stride_ob, stride_oh, stride_od,
+    # Shapes
+    BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, MAX_SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE,
+    HEAD_DIM_PADDED: tl.constexpr,
+    NUM_PAGES: tl.constexpr,
+    PAGE_SIZE_CONST: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_SIZE_D: tl.constexpr,
+    GROUP_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_hkv = tl.program_id(1)
+
+    # Compute seq_len for this batch element
+    seq_len = tl.load(SeqLens + pid_b)
+    num_pages_needed = (seq_len + PAGE_SIZE_CONST - 1) // PAGE_SIZE_CONST
+
+    # Load block table for this batch
+    # block_table[pid_b, :] -> page indices
+    # Load all page indices
+    offs_bt = tl.arange(0, NUM_PAGES)
+    page_indices = tl.load(
+        BlockTable + pid_b * stride_bt_b + offs_bt,
+        mask=offs_bt < num_pages_needed,
+        other=0,
+    )
+
+    # Compute Q pointer for the group of heads
+    # Q[pid_b, pid_hkv * group_size : (pid_hkv+1) * group_size, :]
+    q_base = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + pid_hkv * GROUP_SIZE * stride_qh
+
+    # Output pointer base
+    out_base = Out + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_hkv * GROUP_SIZE * stride_oh
+
+    # Initialize accumulators for each head in the group
+    # We'll process HEAD_DIM_PADDED elements at a time
+    num_d_blocks = HEAD_DIM // BLOCK_SIZE_D
+
+    # Running max and denominator for online softmax (per head in group)
+    # acc_num[group][d]: accumulated numerator
+    # acc_denom[group]: accumulated denominator
+    acc_num = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SIZE_D), dtype=tl.float32)
+    acc_denom = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE,), dtype=tl.float32)
+    acc_max = tl.full((GROUP_SIZE,), -1e30, dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    # Load all Q vectors for the group
+    # q_vecs[group][d_block]
+    offs_d_block = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_SIZE_D)
+    q_ptrs_base = tl.make_block_ptr(
+        base=Q + pid_b * stride_qb,
+        shape=(NUM_HEADS, HEAD_DIM),
+        strides=(stride_qh, stride_qd),
+        offsets=(0, 0),
+        block_shape=(GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SIZE_D),
+        order=(1, 0),
+    )
+
+    # For each head group member, load Q
+    q_group_ptrs = tl.make_block_ptr(
+        base=Q + pid_b * stride_qb,
+        shape=(NUM_HEADS, HEAD_DIM),
+        strides=(stride_qh, stride_qd),
+        offsets=(pid_hkv * GROUP_SIZE, 0),
+        block_shape=(GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SIZE_D),
+        order=(1, 0),
+    )
+    q_vec = tl.load(q_group_ptrs, boundary_check=(0, 1), padding_option="zero")
+    q_vec = q_vec.to(tl.float32)
+
+    # Scale factor
+    scale = 1.0 / tl.sqrt(HEAD_DIM)
+
+    # Iterate over pages
+    for page_idx in range(NUM_PAGES):
+        if page_idx >= num_pages_needed:
+            break
+
+        page_id = tl.load(BlockTable + pid_b * stride_bt_b + page_idx)
+
+        # Compute K and V pointers for this page
+        # kv_cache[page_id, :, pid_hkv, :] -> (page_size, head_dim * 2)
+        page_base = KVC + page_id * stride_kc_b + pid_hkv * stride_kc_h
+
+        # Load K block: (page_size, head_dim)
+        # Then load V block: (page_size, head_dim) starting at head_dim offset
+
+        # Use block pointers for K
+        k_block_ptrs = tl.make_block_ptr(
+            base=page_base,
+            shape=(PAGE_SIZE_CONST, HEAD_DIM),
+            strides=(stride_kc_s, stride_kc_d),
+            offsets=(0, 0),
+            block_shape=(PAGE_SIZE_CONST, BLOCK_SIZE_D),
+            order=(1, 0),
+        )
+        k_block = tl.load(k_block_ptrs, boundary_check=(0, 1), padding_option="zero")
+        k_block = k_block.to(tl.float32)
+
+        # V block
+        v_block_ptrs = tl.make_block_ptr(
+            base=page_base + HEAD_DIM,
+            shape=(PAGE_SIZE_CONST, HEAD_DIM),
+            strides=(stride_kc_s, stride_kc_d),
+            offsets=(0, 0),
+            block_shape=(PAGE_SIZE_CONST, BLOCK_SIZE_D),
+            order=(1, 0),
+        )
+        v_block = tl.load(v_block_ptrs, boundary_check=(0, 1), padding_option="zero")
+        v_block = v_block.to(tl.float32)
+
+        # For each token position in the page:
+        for s in range(PAGE_SIZE_CONST):
+            token_global = page_idx * PAGE_SIZE_CONST + s
+            if token_global >= seq_len:
+                break
+
+            # k_vec: (1, BLOCK_SIZE_D)
+            k_vec = tl.broadcast_to(k_block[s:s+1, :], (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_SIZE_D))
+
+            # QK^T for the group: (GROUP_SIZE,) dot product
+            qk = tl.sum(q_vec * k_vec, axis=1) * scale
+
+            # Online softmax update
+            old_max = acc_max
+            new_max = tl.maximum(old_max, qk)
+            exp_diff = tl.exp(qk - new_max)
+            rescale = tl.exp(old_max - new_max)
+
+            # V contribution
+            v_vec = tl.broadc

... (5541 more chars)
args

  "filePath": "/home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/03_paged_attention/solution.py"

The design: - One CUDA block per batch element per head (or per kv_head group) - GQA: each kv_head's K/V block is shared by `group_size` query heads - For each query head, compute QK^T dot products across all pages, accumulate online softmax with V

import torch
import reference
import solution

B, H, Hkv, D, L, P = 8, 32, 8, 128, 1024, 16
reference.BATCH, reference.NUM_HEADS, reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = B, H, Hkv
reference.HEAD_DIM, reference.SEQ_LEN, reference.PAGE_SIZE = D, L, P

model = solution.Model(B, H, Hkv, D, L, P).cuda().eval()
ref = reference.Model(B, H, Hkv, D, L, P).cuda().eval()

torch.manual_seed(42)
inputs = [t.cuda() for t in reference.get_inputs()]

with torch.no_grad():
    sol_out = model(*inputs)
    ref_out = ref(*inputs)

print('sol shape:', sol_out.shape, ref_out.shape)
print('max abs diff:', (sol_out.float() - ref_out.float()).abs().max().item())
print('atol 0.02:', torch.allclose(sol_out.float(), ref_out.float(), atol=0.02))

@@ -0,0 +1,83 @@
+"""Custom Triton paged attention decode kernel."""
+import math
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+def _make_scale(head_dim: int) -> float:
+    return 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _paged_decode_kernel(
+    Out,
+    Q,
+    KV,
+    BlockTable,
+    SeqLens,
+    # Strides
+    stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_qd,
+    stride_kvb, stride_kvs, stride_kvh, stride_kvd,
+    stride_bt_b,
+    stride_ob, stride_oh, stride_od,
+    # constexpr
+    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
+    HEAD_DIM_PACKED: tl.constexpr,
+    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+    SCALE: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_h = tl.program_id(1)
+
+    pid_hkv = pid_h // num_kv_heads
+
+    seq_len = tl.load(SeqLens + pid_b)
+
+    d_offs = tl.arange(0, HEAD_DIM_PACKED)
+    d_mask = d_offs < HEAD_DIM
+
+    q_ptr = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + pid_h * stride_qh + d_offs * stride_qd
+    q = tl.load(q_ptr, mask=d_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+    acc_num = tl.zeros([HEAD_DIM_PACKED], dtype=tl.float32)
+    acc_denom = 0.0
+    acc_max = -1e30
+
+    bt_base = pid_b * stride_bt_b
+
+    # Compute total tokens for iteration
+    num_pages = (seq_len + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE
+    total_tokens = num_pages * PAGE_SIZE
+
+    for t in tl.range(total_tokens):
+        valid = t < seq_len
+        if valid:
+            page_i = t // PAGE_SIZE
+            s = t % PAGE_SIZE
+
+            page_id = tl.load(BlockTable + bt_base + page_i)
+            page_base = page_id * stride_kvb + pid_hkv * stride_kvh
+
+            k_ptr = KV + page_base + s * stride_kvs + d_offs * stride_kvd
+            k = tl.load(k_ptr, mask=d_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+            qk = tl.sum(q * k) * SCALE
+
+            v_ptr = KV + page_base + s * stride_kvs + (d_offs + HEAD_DIM) * stride_kvd
+            v = tl.load(v_ptr, mask=d_mask, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+            old_max = acc_max
+            new_max = tl.maximum(old_max, qk)
+            exp_val = tl.exp(qk - new_max)
+            rescale_old = tl.exp(old_max - new_max)
+
+            acc_num = acc_num * rescale_old + v * exp_val
+            acc_denom = acc_denom * rescale_old + exp_val
+            acc_max = new_max
+
+    out = acc_num / acc_denom
+
+    out_ptr = Out + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + d_offs * stride_od
+    tl.store(out_ptr, out.to(Out.type.element_ty), mask=d_mask)
args

-"""Custom Triton paged attention decode kernel.
+"""Optimized Triton paged attention decode kernel.
 
 Strategy:
-- One program per (batch, query_head)
-- Each program loads page pointers from block_table for its batch
-- Loads one page of K and V at a time into registers/SRAM
-- Computes qk dot product, online softmax accumulation
-- Uses tl.dot for QK^T and weighted sum
-- GQA: pid_hkv = pid_h // group_size
+- One program per (batch, kv_head)
+- Each program:
+  1. Pre-loads all page indices from block_table for this batch
+  2. Loads entire pages of K and V into SRAM at once (PAGE_SIZE × head_dim blocks)
+  3. For each head in the GQA group, computes QK^T dot products
+  4. Maintains online softmax accumulators per head
+
+This processes all heads in a GQA group together, reducing redundant K/V loads.
+We load K/V pages as full 2D blocks using tl.load, and compute Q@K^T via row-wise dot.
 """
 import math
 import torch

assistant
Good, this is the same as v4 which passed correctness. Now let me think about optimization more carefully. The Triton approach of loading token-by-token is bandwidth-wasteful. The real optimization for paged attention decode is: 1. **Vectorized memory access**: Load entire K and V rows at once (contiguous in D dimension - already done) 2. **Reduce overhead**: Fewer kernel launches by processing multiple heads per program 3. **Coalesced memory**: The KV cache is laid out as (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim*2), so page_base + s*stride_kvs gives us a row where K and V are contiguous The key issue is that Triton loops over MAX_SEQ_LEN are slow because each iteration has control flow. For decode with large seq_len, we need to load multiple tokens per iteration. Let me use a different approach: 1. **Load a page at a time** into registers/SRAM 2. **Compute QK^T for the entire page** at once, then update softmax Let me try switching to CUDA C++ for better performance:
assistant

+"""CUDA C++ paged attention decode kernel using torch.compile/inline PTX.
+
+Strategy:
+- Use torch.compile with custom Triton kernel that loads full page tiles
+- Or use cuda kernel via load_inline
+- One thread block per (batch, kv_head)
+- Each thread handles subset of heads in GQA group + subset of head_dim
+- Load full page K/V into shared memory, process page at a time
+"""
+import math
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+
+
+# We'll write a CUDA kernel and use load_inline
+_kernel_source = """
+#include <cuda_fp16.h>
+#include <cuda_bf16.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+#include <math.h>
+#include <float.h>
+
+#define WARP_SIZE 32
+
+// Paged attention decode kernel.
+// Configuration: (batch, kv_head, head_dim/VEC_SIZE)
+// One warp per (batch, kv_head), threads in warp share K/V loads and compute per-head dot products.
+
+__device__ inline float vec_dot(const nv_bfloat16* a, const nv_bfloat16* b, int d) {
+    float sum = 0.0f;
+    for (int i = 0; i < d; ++i) {
+        float ai = __bfloat162float(a[i]);
+        float bi = __bfloat162float(b[i]);
+        sum += ai * bi;
+    }
+    return sum;
+}
+
+__global__ void paged_decode_kernel(
+    nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ Out,
+    const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ Q,
+    const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ KV,
+    const int32_t* __restrict__ BlockTable,
+    const int32_t* __restrict__ SeqLens,
+    int batch,
+    int num_heads,
+    int num_kv_heads,
+    int head_dim,
+    int page_size,
+    float scale,
+    int stride_qb,
+    int stride_qh,
+    int stride_qd,
+    int stride_kvb,
+    int stride_kvs,
+    int stride_kvh,
+    int stride_kvd,
+    int stride_bt_b,
+    int stride_bt_s,
+    int stride_ob,
+    int stride_oh,
+    int stride_od
+) {
+    int pid_b = blockIdx.x % batch;
+    int pid_hkv = blockIdx.y;
+    int group_start = threadIdx.x;
+    int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads;
+
+    int block_idx_b = blockIdx.x;
+    pid_b = block_idx_b % batch;
+    pid_hkv = blockIdx.y;
+    group_start = threadIdx.x;
+
+    // Each thread in warp handles one head in the GQA group
+    // But only threads with group_start < group_size do work
+
+    // Load seq_len for this batch
+    int seq_len = SeqLens[pid_b];
+    int num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) / page_size;
+
+    // Base pointer for Q
+    int h_base = pid_hkv * group_size;
+
+    // Shared memory for K and V page: (page_size, head_dim) * 2
+    extern __shared__ char smem[];
+    nv_bfloat16* sK = (nv_bfloat16*)smem;
+    nv_bfloat16* sV = sK + page_size * head_dim;
+
+    // Each thread gets its Q vector if within group
+    float q_vec[256]; // max head_dim
+    bool thread_active = (group_start < group_size);
+
+    if (thread_active) {
+        int h = h_base + group_start;
+        const nv_bfloat16* q_ptr = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh;
+        for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d) {
+            q_vec[d] = (float)__bfloat162float(q_ptr[d]);
+        }
+    }
+
+    // Accumulators per thread
+    float acc_num[256];
+    float acc_denom;
+    float acc_max;
+    for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d) acc_num[d] = 0.0f;
+    acc_denom = 1e-30f;
+    acc_max = -1e30f;
+
+    // Process pages
+    for (int page_idx = 0; page_idx < num_pages; ++page_idx) {
+        int block_id = BlockTable[pid_b * stride_bt_b + page_idx * stride_bt_s];
+
+        // Load K and V page into shared memory
+        // Parallelize loading: each thread loads some rows
+        int tokens_per_thread = (page_size + blockDim.x - 1) / blockDim.x;
+        for (int t = 0; t < tokens_per_thread && (threadIdx.x + t) < page_size; ++t) {
+            int tok = threadIdx.x * tokens_per_thread + t;
+            // K row
+            const nv_bfloat16* k_src = KV + block_id * stride_kvb + tok * stride_kvs;
+            nv_bfloat16* k_dst = sK + tok * head_dim;
+            // V row
+            const nv_bfloat16* v_src = k_src + head_dim; // K and V are contiguous
+            nv_bfloat16* v_dst = sV + tok * head_dim;
+
+            for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d) {
+                k_dst[d] = k_src[d];
+                v_dst[d] = v_src[d];
+            }
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+
+        // Each active thread computes QK^T for its head and accumulates
+        if (thread_active) {
+            int num_tokens_in_page = (page_idx + 1) * page_size <= seq_len ? page_size : seq_len - page_idx * page_size;
+
+            for (int tok = 0; tok < num_tokens_in_page; ++tok) {
+                const nv_bfloat16* k_ptr = sK + tok * head_dim;
+                float qk = 0.0f;
+                for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d) {
+                    qk += q_vec[d] * (float)__bfloat162float(k_ptr[d]);
+                }
+                qk *= scale;
+
+                const nv_bfloat16* v_ptr = sV + tok * head_dim;
+
+                float old_max = acc_max;
+                float new_max = fmaxf(old_max, qk);
+                float exp_val = __expf(qk - new_max);
+                float rescale = __expf(old_max - new_max);
+
+                for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d) {
+                    acc_num[d] = acc_num[d] * rescale + exp_val * (float)__bfloat162float(v_ptr[d]);
+                }
+                acc_denom = acc_denom * rescale + exp_val;
+                acc_max = new_max;
+            }
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+    }
+
+    // Compute final output
+    if (thread_active) {
+        int h = h_base + group_start;
+        float inv_denom = 1.0f / acc_denom;
+        nv_bfloat16* out_ptr = Out + pid_b * stride_ob + h * stride_oh;
+        for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d) {
+            out_ptr[d] = __float2bfloat16(acc_num[d] * inv_denom);
+        }
+    }
+}
+"""
+
+
+def _make_scale(head_dim: int) -> float:
+    return 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
+
+
+def _compile_kernel(head_dim: int, page_size: int) -> object:
+    """Compile k

assistant
Let me reconsider the approach. The Triton v4 kernel works correctly but is slow because it processes tokens one-at-a-time. The key optimization is to: 1. **Load entire page tiles** using 2D block pointers into SRAM 2. **Compute QK^T for all tokens in a page at once** using matrix operations 3. **Online softmax update** over the page But Triton's loop restrictions make variable-length loops hard. Let me instead try an approach where I load a whole page of K into a 2D block, compute all QK scores at once, use tl.max and tl.sum for the softmax reduction, and then weight the V values. This is the vLLM approach. Actually, let me try a much more efficient Triton kernel that processes page-at-a-time:

assistant
This is fundamentally the same structure as v4 (token-by-token loop) which will have similar performance. Let me think differently about what actually matters for bandwidth here. The key insight: we're bottlenecked by memory bandwidth. Each token requires loading K (head_dim bf16) and V (head_dim bf16) = 2 * head_dim * 2 bytes = 4 * head_dim bytes. With head_dim=128, that's 512 bytes per token per head. But with GQA, we share K/V across group_size query heads. The real optimization: load a full page of K and V into shared memory / registers ONCE, and have all threads in the GQA group share that load. With Triton, this means one program per (batch, kv_head) instead of per (batch, query_head). Let me write this properly:
assistant

-"""CUDA C++ paged attention decode kernel via torch.compile/extension.
+"""High-performance CUDA paged attention decode kernel.
 
 Strategy:
-- Write raw CUDA kernel and use torch.compile/inline PTX for best performance
 - One thread block per (batch, kv_head)
-- Load K/V pages into shared memory
-- Compute attention for all heads in GQA group sharing the K/V load
+- Each thread handles one head in the GQA group
+- Load each page of K/V into shared memory once
+- All threads in block compute QK^T using their own Q and shared K/V
+- Online softmax accumulation per thread
+- Vectorized memory access for K/V loads
+
+This reduces KV cache bandwidth by sharing K/V loads across a GQA group of heads.
 """
 import math
+import os
 import torch
 import torch.nn as nn
-import triton
-import triton.language as tl
-
-
-# Keep the working Triton kernel as solution, we'll optimize later
+
+
+_CUDA_SOURCE = """
+#include <cuda_fp16.h>
+#include <cuda_bf16.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+#include <math.h>
+
+// Paged attention decode kernel.
+// Grid: (batch, num_kv_heads), Block: (group_size, 1, 1)
+// Each thread handles one query head in the GQA group.
+// Shared memory holds the current page's K and V.
+
+extern "C" __global__
+void __launch_bounds__(1024) paged_decode_kernel(
+    nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ Out,
+    const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ Q,
+    const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ KV,
+    const int* __restrict__ BlockTable,
+    const int* __restrict__ SeqLens,
+    int batch,
+    int num_heads,
+    int num_kv_heads,
+    int head_dim,
+    int page_size,
+    float scale,
+    int stride_qb, int stride_qh, int stride_qd,
+    int stride_kvb, int stride_kvs, int stride_kvh, int stride_kvd,
+    int stride_bt_b, int stride_bt_s,
+    int stride_ob, int stride_oh, int stride_od
+) {
+    // One block per (batch, kv_head)
+    extern __shared__ char smem_ptr[];
+    const int pid_b = blockIdx.x;
+    const int pid_hkv = blockIdx.y;
+    const int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads;
+
+    // Each thread handles one head
+    const int tid = threadIdx.x;
+    const int h = pid_hkv * group_size + tid;
+    const bool is_valid_thread = (tid < group_size);
+
+    // seq_len
+    const int seq_len = SeqLens[pid_b];
+    const int num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) / page_size;
+
+    // Shared memory: K page + V page
+    // K: page_size x head_dim, V: page_size x head_dim
+    nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ smem_k = (nv_bfloat16*)smem_ptr;
+    nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ smem_v = smem_k + page_size * head_dim;
+
+    // Load Q for this thread
+    float q_vec[256]; // max head_dim = 128
+    if (is_valid_thread) {
+        const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ q_base = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh;
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int d = 0; d < 128; d += 8) {
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
+                if ((d + i) < head_dim)
+                    q_vec[d + i] = __bfloat162float(q_base[d + i]);
+            }
+        }
+    }
+
+    // Accumulators
+    float acc_num[256];
+    float acc_denom = 1e-30f;
+    float acc_max = -1e30f;
+    #pragma unroll
+    for (int d = 0; d < 128; ++d) acc_num[d] = 0.0f;
+
+    // Process each page
+    for (int page_idx = 0; page_idx < num_pages; ++page_idx) {
+        const int block_id = BlockTable[pid_b * stride_bt_b + page_idx * stride_bt_s];
+
+        // Load K and V page into shared memory (coalesced across threads)
+        const int tokens_per_thread = (page_size + group_size - 1) / group_size;
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int t_local = 0; t_local < 16; ++t_local) {  // max page_size=16 tokens_per_thread=1 at most
+            const int tok_idx = tid * tokens_per_thread + t_local;
+            if (tok_idx < page_size) {
+                const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ k_src = KV + block_id * stride_kvb + tok_idx * stride_kvs;
+                nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ k_dst = smem_k + tok_idx * head_dim;
+                // K and V are contiguous: V is right after K
+                const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ v_src = k_src + head_dim;
+                nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ v_dst = smem_v + tok_idx * head_dim;
+                #pragma unroll
+                for (int d = 0; d < 128; d += 8) {
+                    #pragma unroll
+                    for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
+                        if ((d + i) < head_dim) {
+                            k_dst[d + i] = k_src[d + i];
+                            v_dst[d + i] = v_src[d + i];
+                        }
+                    }
+                }
+            }
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+
+        // Each thread computes attention for its head using shared K/V
+        if (is_valid_thread) {
+            const int tokens_in_page = (page_idx + 1) * page_size <= seq_len
+                ? page_size : seq_len - page_idx * page_size;
+
+            for (int tok = 0; tok < page_size; ++tok) {
+                if (tok >= tokens_in_page) break;
+
+                // Load K row from shared memory
+                const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ k_row = smem_k + tok * head_dim;
+                float qk = 0.0f;
+                #pragma unroll
+                for (int d = 0; d < 128; d += 8) {
+                    #pragma unroll
+                    for (int i = 0; i < 8; ++i) {
+                        if ((d + i) < head_dim) {
+                            qk += q_vec[d + i] * __bfloat162float(k_row[d + i]);
+                        }
+                    }
+                }
+                qk *= scale;
+
+                // Load V row from shared memory
+                const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ v_row = smem_v + tok * head_dim;
+
+                // Online softmax
+                const float old_max = acc_max;
+

OK good, CUDA 13.2 available. Now let me write a high-performance CUDA kernel. The approach: 1. **One thread block per `(batch, kv_head)`** 2. **Each thread handles one query head** in the GQA group 3. **Load K/V pages into shared memory**, then compute QK^T for all threads' heads 4. **Online softmax** with per-thread accumulator 5. **Vectorized memory operations** for loading K/V This way K/V loads are shared across the GQA group, saving bandwidth.

-"""Paged attention decode kernel using optimized PyTorch tensor operations.
+"""High-performance CUDA paged attention decode kernel via torch.utils.cpp_extension.
 
 Strategy:
-- Gather all K/V pages at once using advanced indexing
-- Reshape to (batch, seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) for K and V
-- Use broadcasted einsum for QK^T and attention
-- Repeat interleave for GQA
-- This is essentially the reference but without Python loops over batch
-- All operations done in fused tensor form on GPU
+- One thread block per (batch, kv_head)
+- Each thread handles one head in the GQA group
+- Load each page of K/V into shared memory once
+- All threads compute QK^T using shared K/V (saves KV bandwidth)
+- Online softmax per thread
 """
 import math
 import torch
 import torch.nn as nn
+from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline
+
+def _make_scale(head_dim: int) -> float:
+    return 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
+
+_CUDA_SRC = r"""
+#include <cuda_fp16.h>
+#include <cuda_bf16.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+
+__global__ void __launch_bounds__(512) paged_decode_kernel(
+    nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ Out,
+    const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ Q,
+    const nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ KV,
+    const int* __restrict__ BlockTable,
+    const int* __restrict__ SeqLens,
+    int batch, int num_heads, int num_kv_heads, int head_dim,
+    int page_size, float scale,
+    int stride_qb, int stride_qh, int stride_qd,
+    int stride_kvb, int stride_kvs, int stride_kvh, int stride_kvd,
+    int stride_bt_b, int stride_bt_s,
+    int stride_ob, int stride_oh, int stride_od
+) {
+    int pid_b = blockIdx.x;
+    int pid_hkv = blockIdx.y;
+    int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads;
+    int tid = threadIdx.x;
+
+    if (tid >= group_size) return;
+
+    int h = pid_hkv * group_size + tid;
+    int seq_len = SeqLens[pid_b];
+    int num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) / page_size;
+
+    // Shared memory for current page K + V
+    extern __shared__ char smem[];
+    nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ sK = (nv_bfloat16*)smem;
+    nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ sV = sK + page_size * head_dim;
+
+    // Load Q
+    float q[128];
+    const nv_bfloat16* qp = Q + pid_b * stride_qb + h * stride_qh;
+    for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d)
+        q[d] = __bfloat162float(qp[d]);
+
+    // Accumulators
+    float acc_num[128] = {0};
+    float acc_denom = 1e-30f;
+    float acc_max = -1e30f;
+
+    for (int pg = 0; pg < num_pages; ++pg) {
+        int block_id = BlockTable[pid_b * stride_bt_b + pg * stride_bt_s];
+
+        // Cooperative load of K/V page
+        const nv_bfloat16* k_page_src = KV + block_id * stride_kvb;
+        const int tokens_to_load = page_size;
+        const int items_thread = (tokens_to_load * head_dim + group_size - 1) / group_size;
+
+        for (int i_idx = 0; i_idx < items_thread; ++i_idx) {
+            int flat = tid * items_thread + i_idx;
+            if (flat < tokens_to_load * head_dim) {
+                int row = flat / head_dim;
+                int col = flat % head_dim;
+                // K
+                sK[row * head_dim + col] = k_page_src[row * stride_kvs + col * stride_kvd];
+                // V (contiguous after K in last dim)
+                sV[row * head_dim + col] = k_page_src[row * stride_kvs + head_dim + col * stride_kvd];
+            }
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+
+        // Compute attention for tokens in this page
+        int tokens_in_page = (pg + 1) * page_size <= seq_len ? page_size : seq_len - pg * page_size;
+        for (int t = 0; t < tokens_in_page; ++t) {
+            float qk = 0.0f;
+            const nv_bfloat16* kr = sK + t * head_dim;
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int d = 0; d < 128; ++d) {
+                if (d < head_dim) qk += q[d] * __bfloat162float(kr[d]);
+            }
+            qk *= scale;
+
+            float old_max = acc_max;
+            float new_max = fmaxf(old_max, qk);
+            float exp_v = __expf(qk - new_max);
+            float rescale = __expf(old_max - new_max);
+
+            const nv_bfloat16* vr = sV + t * head_dim;
+            for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d) {
+                acc_num[d] = acc_num[d] * rescale + exp_v * __bfloat162float(vr[d]);
+            }
+            acc_denom = acc_denom * rescale + exp_v;
+            acc_max = new_max;
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+    }
+
+    // Write output
+    nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ op = Out + pid_b * stride_ob + h * stride_oh;
+    float inv = 1.0f / acc_denom;
+    for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; ++d)
+        op[d] = __float2bfloat16(acc_num[d] * inv);
+}
+"""
+
+_CPP_SRC = r"""
+#include <torch/extension.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+
+void paged_decode_forward(
+    torch::Tensor out,
+    torch::Tensor query,
+    torch::Tensor kv_cache,
+    torch::Tensor block_table,
+    torch::Tensor seq_lens,
+    float scale) {
+
+    int B = query.size(0);
+    int H = query.size(1);
+    int Hkv = kv_cache.size(2);
+    int D = query.size(2);
+    int P = kv_cache.size(1);  // page_size
+    int G = H / Hkv;
+
+    int smem_size = 2 * P * D * 2;  // K + V in bf16
+
+    int gridX = B;
+    int gridY = Hkv;
+    int blockZ = G;
+
+    paged_decode_kernel<<<dim3(gridX, gridY, 1), dim3(blockZ, 1, 1), smem_size>>>(
+        (nv_bfloat16*)out.data_ptr(),
+        (const nv_bfloat16*)query.data_ptr(),
+        (const nv_bfloat16*)kv_cache.data_ptr(),
+        block_table.data_ptr<int>(),
+        seq_lens.data_ptr<int>(),
+        B, H, Hkv, D, P, scale,
+        query.stride(0), query.stride(1), query.stride(2),
+        kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2), kv_cache.stride(3),
+        block_table.stride(0), block_table.stride(1),
+        out.stride(0), out.stride(1), out.stride(2)
+    );
+}
+
+PYBIND11_MODULE(TORCH_EXTENSION

prompt (4259 chars — TRUNCATED)
Write an optimized Triton paged attention decode kernel for SM120 Blackwell GPUs. The kernel should be written to `/home/infatoshi/cuda/KernelBench-Hard/problems/03_paged_attention/solution.py`.

**Requirements:**
- Input: query (batch, num_heads, head_dim) bf16, kv_cache (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim*2) bf16, block_table (batch, max_blocks) int32, seq_lens (batch,) int32
- Output: bf16 (batch, num_heads, head_dim)
- GQA: num_heads / num_kv_heads may be > 1 (group_size)
- Must handle all shapes listed below
- Correctness tolerance: 0.02 abs/rel on bf16

**Shapes:**
1. batch=8, num_heads=32, num_kv_heads=8, head_dim=128, seq_len=1024, page_size=16
2. batch=32, num_heads=32, num_kv_heads=8, head_dim=128, seq_len=2048, page_size=16
3. batch=4, num_heads=64, num_kv_heads=8, head_dim=128, seq_len=4096, page_size=16
4. batch=16, num_heads=32, num_kv_heads=8, head_dim=128, seq_len=1535, page_size=16
5. batch=8, num_heads=16, num_kv_heads=4, head_dim=64, seq_len=2000, page_size=16

**Important Triton notes:**
1. `tl.range` with non-constexpr bounds works but `break`/`continue` are NOT supported - use if/else with masking instead
2. Simultaneous multiple assignment is NOT supported (don't do `a, b = x, y`)
3. Use constexpr for known sizes like HEAD_DIM, PAGE_SIZE passed from Python
4. The kernel must handle variable seq_len via predication (masking)

**Performance strategy:**
- One program per (batch, query_head)
- Since head_dim <= 128, load 128 elements at once for K and V (contiguous in last dim)
- Each iteration loads ONE token's K and V (128 bf16 values each)
- Use vectorized loads (single tl.load with 128-element range)
- Accumulate online softmax

**Reference reference implementation:**
```python
# For each batch b:
#   Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element
#   Repeat KV heads for GQA
#   scores = Q @ K^T / sqrt(d)  -> softmax -> scores @ V
```

**Critical correctness rule:** When `t >= seq_len`, the QK score must NOT affect the softmax. Use masking: set qk = -1e30 for invalid tokens.

**Key insight for correctness:** The initial acc_max is -1e30. When the first valid token arrives with qk, exp(qk - max(-1e30, qk)) should work correctly. The issue is: if the very first token is INVALID with qk=-1e30, then new_max=-1e30, exp(0)=1, which would incorrectly add to acc_num with v=0 (since v is masked with other=0). This is actually OK because v=0 so it doesn't affect results. BUT if multiple invalid tokens come first, exp_val=1 every time and acc_denom grows. When a valid token appears, rescale = exp(-1e30 - new_max) ~ 0, so the accumulated garbage is zeroed out. So the math should work out.

However, there's a numerical edge case: if ONLY invalid tokens exist, acc_denom could be large and acc_num = 0, giving output 0. This shouldn't happen since seq_len > 0.

**Write the complete solution.py file with:**
1. The Triton kernel `_paged_decode_kernel` 
2. `Model` class with `__init__` and `forward`
3. `get_inputs()` and `get_init_inputs()` that delegate to reference module

The Model class should:
- Compute scale = 1/sqrt(head_dim)
- Pass all parameters as constexpr (HEAD_DIM, PAGE_SIZE, etc.) to the Triton kernel
- Use grid = (B, H) where B=batch and H=num_heads

**IMPORTANT:** Make sure the kernel is CORRECT first. I've verified that the following simple structure works:
```python
for t in tl.range(max_tokens):
    valid = t < seq_len
    page_i = t // PAGE_SIZE
    s = t % PAGE_SIZE
    page_id = tl.load(BlockTable + bt_base + page_i * stride_bt_s)
    page_base = page_id * stride_kvb + pid_hkv * stride_kvh
    # Load K
    k = tl.load(KV + page_base + s * stride_kvs + d_offs * stride_kvd, mask=d_mask & valid, other=0.0)
    qk = tl.sum(q * k) * SCALE
    # Load V  
    v = tl.load(KV + page_base + s * stride_kvs + (d_offs + HEAD_DIM) * stride_kvd, mask=d_mask & valid, other=0.0)
    qk = tl.where(valid, qk, -1e30)
    # Online softmax update...
```

Help on function load in module triton.language.core:

load(pointer, mask=None, other=None, boundary_check=(), padding_option='', cache_modifier='', eviction_policy='', volatile=False, _semantic=None)
    Return a tensor of data whose values are loaded from memory at location defined by `pointer`:

        (1) If `pointer` is a single element pointer, a scalar is be loaded.  In
            this case:

            - `mask` and `other` must also be scalars,
            - `other` is implicitly typecast to `pointer.dtype.element_ty`, and
            - `boundary_check` and `padding_option` must be empty.

        (2) If `pointer` is an N-dimensional tensor of pointers, an
            N-dimensional tensor is loaded.  In this case:

            - `mask` and `other` are implicitly broadcast to `pointer.shape`,
            - `other` is implicitly typecast to `pointer.dtype.element_ty`, and
            - `boundary_check` and `padding_option` must be empty.

        (3) If `pointer` is a block pointer defined by `make_block_ptr`, a
            tensor is loaded.  In this case:

            - `mask` and `other` must be `None`, and
            - `boundary_check` and `padding_option` can be specified to control the behavior of out-of-bound access.

    :param pointer: Pointer to the data to be loaded
    :type pointer: `triton.PointerType`, or block of `dtype=triton.PointerType`
    :param mask: if `mask[idx]` is false, do not load the data at address `pointer[idx]`
        (must be `None`

+__global__ void paged_decode_kernel(
+    bfloat* __restrict__ Out,

The CUDA kernel is very slow! The problem is that we're launching tiny thread blocks (group_size=4 threads) which massively underutilize the GPU. Let me redesign the kernel: 1. **One thread block per (batch, head)** - more parallelism 2. **Load K/V page into shared memory with full warp utilization** - all 32 threads cooperate 3. **Use a single thread within the block per head computation** Actually, the real issue: group_size=4 means 4 threads per block, which is tiny. We need 128-256 threads per block to saturate SMs. Let me redesign: one block per (batch, head), load K/V page cooperatively, and compute within each block:

assistant
The issue is clear now: we're loading K/V for each (batch, kv_head) block independently. Each page's KV cache is loaded GROUP_SIZE times (once per batch,kv_head block). For GQA with group_size=4, K/V data gets loaded 4x more than necessary. Let me reconsider the architecture. The fundamental problem with paged decode: - Memory bandwidth is the bottleneck (KV cache is streamed once) - We need to avoid redundant K/V loads The right approach for SM120 Blackwell is actually different: use **per (batch, query_head) blocks** with optimized memory access patterns. Each thread loads its own K/V and computes its attention. The key optimizations: 1. **Use `__ldg` (read-only data cache)** for K accesses - they're read-only 2. **Use `float4` / `float2` vector loads** for K/V 3. **Unroll the inner loop** over head_dim 4. **Use `__shfl` reductions** instead of shared memory for qk reduction** But wait - for `group_size=4` with 128-thread blocks, we're only using 4 threads per block. For `group_size=8`, that's only 8 threads. The GPU has 188 SMs, and we need to saturate all of them. Actually, for shape 0: B=8, Hkv=8 => 64 blocks. For shape 1: B=32, Hkv=8 => 256 blocks. With 128 threads each, that's only 8192 threads for shape 1 - well under saturation. The real issue: **too few parallelism**. We should use **one block per (batch, query_head)** for massive parallelism:
assistant
in 116045out 804cache_r 0cache_w 0
assistant
With `grid(b,h)`, we get 128-1024 blocks, each computing one head. With 128 threads each, that's 16K-131K threads. With `grid(b,kv)`, only 32-256 blocks (4K-32K threads). Neither is saturating 188 SMs with thousands of threads each. But here's the key: decode is **memory bound**, not compute bound. The metric is **bandwidth** utilization. With per-head blocks: - Each block loads K/V independently → K/V loaded GROUP_SIZE times → 4x bandwidth wasted - But we get 4x more parallelism → may still be better for hiding latency With per-kv-head blocks: - K/V loaded once per group → save bandwidth - But only GROUP_SIZE threads in block → underutilized SMs Actually let me re-examine: the per-kv-head kernel should be loading K/V ONCE and then reusing across the group. The problem is: we're launching small blocks (4-8 threads) which can't saturate SMs. But that should be OK because SMs can run many small blocks concurrently. Wait, the REAL issue might be that with `launch_bounds__(128)` but only 4-8 threads, the compiler generates terrible code. Let me check:

import torch
import reference
import solution

B, H, Hkv, D, L, P = 8, 32, 8, 128, 1024, 16

ref = reference.Model(B, H, Hkv, D, L, P).cuda().eval()

# Time each call
import time

end = torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True)

torch.cuda.synchronize()
start.record()
with torch.no_grad():
    sol_out = model(*inputs)
end.record()
torch.cuda.synchronize()

with torch.no_grad():
    ref_out = ref(*inputs)
end.record()

The kernel is 3x faster than the reference but still slow. Let me investigate: the kernel launch uses 128 threads per block but only `group_size` threads actually compute (the `is_worker` check). So 124 out of 128 threads just load K/V. This means: 1. For shape 0: 64 blocks × 128 threads = 8192 threads total, but only 64 × 4 = 256 do computation 2. The K/V loading is 97% of threads, but it should be a tiny fraction of work The real bottleneck: **every block loads the SAME K/V page data into its OWN shared memory**. Across B×Hkv blocks, each K/V token is loaded H / Hkv = GROUP_SIZE times total. No actual sharing! Let me redesign: use one block per (batch, query_head) but with each block loading only what it needs (no shared memory, each thread loads its own K/V from global memory with read-only cache). This is bandwidth-heavy but we get more parallelism:

newString (2119 chars)
    CPP_SRC = r"""
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda_bf16.h>

// Kernel declaration (defined in .cu)
__global__ void paged_decode_kernel(
    __nv_bfloat16* Out, const __nv_bfloat16* Q, const __nv_bfloat16* KV,
    const int* BlockTable, const int* SeqLens,
    int B, int H, int Hkv, int D, int P, float scale,
    int stride_qb, int stride_qo,
    int stride_kvb, int stride_kvs, int stride_kvh, int stride_kvo,
    int stride_ob, int stride_oo,
    int stride_bt_row);

void launch_paged_decode(
    __nv_bfloat16* Out, const __nv_bfloat16* Q, const __nv_bfloat16* KV,
    const int* BlockTable, const int* SeqLens,
    int B, int H, int Hkv, int D, int P, float scale,
    int stride_bt_row,
    int stride_qb, int stride_qo,
    int stride_kvb, int stride_kvs, int stride_kvh, int stride_kvo,
    int stride_ob, int stride_oo
) {
    dim3 grid(B, H);
    dim3 block(128, 1, 1);
    paged_decode_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(
        Out, Q, KV, BlockTable, SeqLens,
        B, H, Hkv, D, P, scale,
        stride_qb, stride_qo,
        stride_kvb, stride_kvs, stride_kvh, stride_kvo,
        stride_ob, stride_oo, stride_bt_row);
}

void paged_attention_forward(
    torch::Tensor out,
    torch::Tensor query,
    torch::Tensor kv_cache,
    torch::Tensor block_table,
    torch::Tensor seq_lens,
    float scale)
{
    int B = query.size(0);
    int H = query.size(1);
    int D = query.size(2);
    int Hkv = kv_cache.size(2);
    int P = kv_cache.size(1);
    int stride_bt_row = block_table.stride(0);

    launch_paged_decode(
        (__nv_bfloat16*)out.data_ptr(),
        (const __nv_bfloat16*)query.data_ptr(),
        (const __nv_bfloat16*)kv_cache.data_ptr(),
        block_table.data_ptr<int>(),
        seq_lens.data_ptr<int>(),
        B, H, Hkv, D, P, scale,
        stride_bt_row,
        query.stride(0), query.stride(1),
        kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2), kv_cache.stride(3),
        out.stride(0), out.stride(1));
}

PYBIND11_MODULE(TORCH_EXTENSION_NAME, m) {
    m.def("paged_attention_forward", &paged_attention_forward, "paged_attention_forward");
}
"""

void launch_paged_decode(
    bfloat* Out, const bfloat* Q, const bfloat* KV,
    const int* BlockTable, const int* SeqLens,
    int B, int H, int Hkv, int D, int P, float scale,
    int stride_bt_row,
    int stride_qb, int stride_qo,
    int stride_kvb, int stride_kvs, int stride_kvh, int stride_kvo,

) {
    dim3 grid(B, H);
    dim3 block(128, 1, 1);
    paged_decode_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(
        Out, Q, KV, BlockTable, SeqLens,
        B, H, Hkv, D, P, scale,
        stride_qb, stride_qo,
        stride_kvb, stride_kvs, stride_kvh, stride_kvo,
        stride_ob, stride_oo, stride_bt_row);
}

void paged_attention_forward(
    torch::Tensor out,
    torch::Tensor query,
    torch::Tensor kv_cache,
    torch::Tensor block_table,
    torch::Tensor seq_lens,
    float scale)
{
    int B = query.size(0);
    int H = query.size(1);
    int D = query.size(2);
    int Hkv = kv_cache.size(2);
    int P = kv_cache.size(1);
    int stride_bt_row = block_table.stride(0);

    launch_paged_decode(
        (__nv_bfloat16*)out.data_ptr(),
        (const __nv_bfloat16*)query.data_ptr(),
        (const __nv_bfloat16*)kv_cache.data_ptr(),
        block_table.data_ptr<int>(),
        seq_lens.data_ptr<int>(),
        B, H, Hkv, D, P, scale,
        stride_bt_row,
        query.stride(0), query.stride(1),
        kv_cache.stride(0), kv_cache.stride(1), kv_cache.stride(2), kv_cache.stride(3),
        out.stride(0), out.stride(1));
}

PYBIND11_MODULE(TORCH_EXTENSION_NAME, m) {
    m.def("paged_attention_forward", &paged_attention_forward, "paged_attention_forward");
}
